\mbox{\Hypertarget{libusb_8h_aa7d6035eb2692d455d27144560a0f68d}\label{libusb_8h_aa7d6035eb2692d455d27144560a0f68d}} 
\index{libusb.h@{libusb.h}!LIBUSB\_CALL@{LIBUSB\_CALL}}
\index{LIBUSB\_CALL@{LIBUSB\_CALL}!libusb.h@{libusb.h}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{LIBUSB\_CALL}{LIBUSB\_CALL}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \#define LIBUSB\+\_\+\+CALL}

libusbx\textquotesingle{}s Windows calling convention.

Under Windows, the selection of available compilers and configurations means that, unlike other platforms, there is not {\itshape one true calling convention} (calling convention\+: the manner in which parameters are passed to funcions in the generated assembly code).

Matching the Windows API itself, libusbx uses the WINAPI convention (which translates to the {\ttfamily stdcall} convention) and guarantees that the library is compiled in this way. The public header file also includes appropriate annotations so that your own software will use the right convention, even if another convention is being used by default within your codebase.

The one consideration that you must apply in your software is to mark all functions which you use as libusbx callbacks with this LIBUSB\+\_\+\+CALL annotation, so that they too get compiled for the correct calling convention.

On non-\/\+Windows operating systems, this macro is defined as nothing. This means that you can apply it to your code without worrying about cross-\/platform compatibility. \mbox{\Hypertarget{libusb_8h_af39dc5e7622e8559df7f1d3da5478717}\label{libusb_8h_af39dc5e7622e8559df7f1d3da5478717}} 
\index{libusb.h@{libusb.h}!LIBUSB\_CONTROL\_SETUP\_SIZE@{LIBUSB\_CONTROL\_SETUP\_SIZE}}
\index{LIBUSB\_CONTROL\_SETUP\_SIZE@{LIBUSB\_CONTROL\_SETUP\_SIZE}!libusb.h@{libusb.h}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{LIBUSB\_CONTROL\_SETUP\_SIZE}{LIBUSB\_CONTROL\_SETUP\_SIZE}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \#define LIBUSB\+\_\+\+CONTROL\+\_\+\+SETUP\+\_\+\+SIZE~(sizeof(struct \mbox{\hyperlink{structlibusb__control__setup}{libusb\+\_\+control\+\_\+setup}}))}

{\footnotesize\ttfamily \#define libusb\+\_\+le16\+\_\+to\+\_\+cpu~libusb\+\_\+cpu\+\_\+to\+\_\+le16}

\mbox{\Hypertarget{libusb_8h_aa83ecded256e0767220bcc21cc92365d}\label{libusb_8h_aa83ecded256e0767220bcc21cc92365d}} 
\index{libusb.h@{libusb.h}!LIBUSBX\_API\_VERSION@{LIBUSBX\_API\_VERSION}}
\index{LIBUSBX\_API\_VERSION@{LIBUSBX\_API\_VERSION}!libusb.h@{libusb.h}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{LIBUSBX\_API\_VERSION}{LIBUSBX\_API\_VERSION}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \#define LIBUSBX\+\_\+\+API\+\_\+\+VERSION~0x01000102}

libusbx\textquotesingle{}s API version.

Since version 1.\+0.\+13, to help with feature detection, libusbx defines a LIBUSBX\+\_\+\+API\+\_\+\+VERSION macro that gets increased every time there is a significant change to the API, such as the introduction of a new call, the definition of a new macro/enum member, or any other element that libusbx applications may want to detect at compilation time.

The macro is typically used in an application as follows\+: 
\begin{DoxyCode}{0}
\DoxyCodeLine{\textcolor{preprocessor}{\#if defined(LIBUSBX\_API\_VERSION) \&\& (LIBUSBX\_API\_VERSION >= 0x01001234)}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\textcolor{comment}{// Use one of the newer features from the libusbx API}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\textcolor{preprocessor}{\#endif}}

\end{DoxyCode}


Another feature of LIBUSBX\+\_\+\+API\+\_\+\+VERSION is that it can be used to detect whether you are compiling against the libusb or the libusbx library.

Internally, LIBUSBX\+\_\+\+API\+\_\+\+VERSION is defined as follows\+: (libusbx major \texorpdfstring{$<$}{<}\texorpdfstring{$<$}{<} 24) $\vert$ (libusbx minor \texorpdfstring{$<$}{<}\texorpdfstring{$<$}{<} 16) $\vert$ (16 bit incremental) 

\doxysubsection{Typedef Documentation}
\mbox{\Hypertarget{libusb_8h_a4ec088aa7b79c4a9599e39bf36a72833}\label{libusb_8h_a4ec088aa7b79c4a9599e39bf36a72833}} 
\index{libusb.h@{libusb.h}!libusb\_context@{libusb\_context}}
\index{libusb\_context@{libusb\_context}!libusb.h@{libusb.h}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{libusb\_context}{libusb\_context}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily typedef struct \mbox{\hyperlink{libusb_8h_a4ec088aa7b79c4a9599e39bf36a72833}{libusb\+\_\+context}} \mbox{\hyperlink{libusb_8h_a4ec088aa7b79c4a9599e39bf36a72833}{libusb\+\_\+context}}}

Structure representing a libusbx session. The concept of individual libusbx sessions allows for your program to use two libraries (or dynamically load two modules) which both independently use libusb. This will prevent interference between the individual libusbx users -\/ for example \mbox{\hyperlink{libusb_8h_ab4974e3de2973e8241801f2136805749}{libusb\+\_\+set\+\_\+debug()}} will not affect the other user of the library, and \mbox{\hyperlink{libusb_8h_aa9ff0ee5b1580833ad2e23eaa89529f0}{libusb\+\_\+exit()}} will not destroy resources that the other user is still using.

Sessions are created by \mbox{\hyperlink{libusb_8h_a7c69ac34aaf043c495a9e0914662bc5f}{libusb\+\_\+init()}} and destroyed through \mbox{\hyperlink{libusb_8h_aa9ff0ee5b1580833ad2e23eaa89529f0}{libusb\+\_\+exit()}}. If your application is guaranteed to only ever include a single libusbx user (i.\+e. you), you do not have to worry about contexts\+: pass NULL in every function call where a context is required. The default context will be used.

For more information, see contexts. \mbox{\Hypertarget{libusb_8h_a77eedd00d01eb7569b880e861a971c2b}\label{libusb_8h_a77eedd00d01eb7569b880e861a971c2b}} 
\index{libusb.h@{libusb.h}!libusb\_device@{libusb\_device}}
\index{libusb\_device@{libusb\_device}!libusb.h@{libusb.h}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{libusb\_device}{libusb\_device}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily typedef struct \mbox{\hyperlink{libusb_8h_a77eedd00d01eb7569b880e861a971c2b}{libusb\+\_\+device}} \mbox{\hyperlink{libusb_8h_a77eedd00d01eb7569b880e861a971c2b}{libusb\+\_\+device}}}

Structure representing a USB device detected on the system. This is an opaque type for which you are only ever provided with a pointer, usually originating from \mbox{\hyperlink{libusb_8h_a6621130c99cc8f299d47901568dac7c2}{libusb\+\_\+get\+\_\+device\+\_\+list()}}.

Certain operations can be performed on a device, but in order to do any I/O you will have to first obtain a device handle using \mbox{\hyperlink{libusb_8h_a2aad4916668a37ae3fa77a1b1ca817bd}{libusb\+\_\+open()}}.

Devices are reference counted with \mbox{\hyperlink{libusb_8h_a8b4c51faab58367d79f814286b2d220c}{libusb\+\_\+ref\+\_\+device()}} and \mbox{\hyperlink{libusb_8h_aaf10116272e2c71121b6e09717305adc}{libusb\+\_\+unref\+\_\+device()}}, and are freed when the reference count reaches 0. New devices presented by \mbox{\hyperlink{libusb_8h_a6621130c99cc8f299d47901568dac7c2}{libusb\+\_\+get\+\_\+device\+\_\+list()}} have a reference count of 1, and \mbox{\hyperlink{libusb_8h_abb12b7139b9965bed377721762bb3437}{libusb\+\_\+free\+\_\+device\+\_\+list()}} can optionally decrease the reference count on all devices in the list. \mbox{\hyperlink{libusb_8h_a2aad4916668a37ae3fa77a1b1ca817bd}{libusb\+\_\+open()}} adds another reference which is later destroyed by \mbox{\hyperlink{libusb_8h_a6b8983695e63168a3d1e03e2d4def0e8}{libusb\+\_\+close()}}. \mbox{\Hypertarget{libusb_8h_a7df95821d20d27b5597f1d783749d6a4}\label{libusb_8h_a7df95821d20d27b5597f1d783749d6a4}} 
\index{libusb.h@{libusb.h}!libusb\_device\_handle@{libusb\_device\_handle}}
\index{libusb\_device\_handle@{libusb\_device\_handle}!libusb.h@{libusb.h}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{libusb\_device\_handle}{libusb\_device\_handle}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily typedef struct \mbox{\hyperlink{libusb_8h_a7df95821d20d27b5597f1d783749d6a4}{libusb\+\_\+device\+\_\+handle}} \mbox{\hyperlink{libusb_8h_a7df95821d20d27b5597f1d783749d6a4}{libusb\+\_\+device\+\_\+handle}}}

Structure representing a handle on a USB device. This is an opaque type for which you are only ever provided with a pointer, usually originating from \mbox{\hyperlink{libusb_8h_a2aad4916668a37ae3fa77a1b1ca817bd}{libusb\+\_\+open()}}.

A device handle is used to perform I/O and other operations. When finished with a device handle, you should call \mbox{\hyperlink{libusb_8h_a6b8983695e63168a3d1e03e2d4def0e8}{libusb\+\_\+close()}}. \mbox{\Hypertarget{libusb_8h_a34e9904eb8e5124057a866f777cc99a8}\label{libusb_8h_a34e9904eb8e5124057a866f777cc99a8}} 
\index{libusb.h@{libusb.h}!libusb\_hotplug\_callback\_fn@{libusb\_hotplug\_callback\_fn}}
\index{libusb\_hotplug\_callback\_fn@{libusb\_hotplug\_callback\_fn}!libusb.h@{libusb.h}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{libusb\_hotplug\_callback\_fn}{libusb\_hotplug\_callback\_fn}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily typedef int(\mbox{\hyperlink{libusb_8h_aa7d6035eb2692d455d27144560a0f68d}{LIBUSB\+\_\+\+CALL}} $\ast$ libusb\+\_\+hotplug\+\_\+callback\+\_\+fn) (\mbox{\hyperlink{libusb_8h_a4ec088aa7b79c4a9599e39bf36a72833}{libusb\+\_\+context}} $\ast$ctx, \mbox{\hyperlink{libusb_8h_a77eedd00d01eb7569b880e861a971c2b}{libusb\+\_\+device}} $\ast$device, \mbox{\hyperlink{libusb_8h_a556d598ca379618a41bbec3597f55dcf}{libusb\+\_\+hotplug\+\_\+event}} event, \mbox{\hyperlink{libusb_8h_a8ca3594d1761da8da91be2851f4e8f21}{void}} $\ast$user\+\_\+data)}

Hotplug callback function type. When requesting hotplug event notifications, you pass a pointer to a callback function of this type.

This callback may be called by an internal event thread and as such it is recommended the callback do minimal processing before returning.

libusbx will call this function later, when a matching event had happened on a matching device. See hotplug for more information.

It is safe to call either \mbox{\hyperlink{libusb_8h_a54961ed4615afb54c8cf50236b2e40d0}{libusb\+\_\+hotplug\+\_\+register\+\_\+callback()}} or \mbox{\hyperlink{libusb_8h_afe4401894825a2671daa78cbf7094f55}{libusb\+\_\+hotplug\+\_\+deregister\+\_\+callback()}} from within a callback function.

Since version 1.\+0.\+16, \mbox{\hyperlink{libusb_8h_aa83ecded256e0767220bcc21cc92365d}{LIBUSBX\+\_\+\+API\+\_\+\+VERSION}} \texorpdfstring{$>$}{>}= 0x01000102


\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
{\em ctx} & context of this notification \\
\hline
{\em device} & libusb\+\_\+device this event occurred on \\
\hline
{\em event} & event that occurred \\
\hline
{\em user\+\_\+data} & user data provided when this callback was registered \\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
bool whether this callback is finished processing events. returning 1 will cause this callback to be deregistered 
\end{DoxyReturn}
\mbox{\Hypertarget{libusb_8h_a4868157346bbf2c70b6af0cb0a6c0094}\label{libusb_8h_a4868157346bbf2c70b6af0cb0a6c0094}} 
\index{libusb.h@{libusb.h}!libusb\_hotplug\_callback\_handle@{libusb\_hotplug\_callback\_handle}}
\index{libusb\_hotplug\_callback\_handle@{libusb\_hotplug\_callback\_handle}!libusb.h@{libusb.h}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{libusb\_hotplug\_callback\_handle}{libusb\_hotplug\_callback\_handle}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily typedef int \mbox{\hyperlink{libusb_8h_a4868157346bbf2c70b6af0cb0a6c0094}{libusb\+\_\+hotplug\+\_\+callback\+\_\+handle}}}

Callback handle.

Callbacks handles are generated by \mbox{\hyperlink{libusb_8h_a54961ed4615afb54c8cf50236b2e40d0}{libusb\+\_\+hotplug\+\_\+register\+\_\+callback()}} and can be used to deregister callbacks. Callback handles are unique per libusb\+\_\+context and it is safe to call \mbox{\hyperlink{libusb_8h_afe4401894825a2671daa78cbf7094f55}{libusb\+\_\+hotplug\+\_\+deregister\+\_\+callback()}} on an already deregisted callback.

Since version 1.\+0.\+16, \mbox{\hyperlink{libusb_8h_aa83ecded256e0767220bcc21cc92365d}{LIBUSBX\+\_\+\+API\+\_\+\+VERSION}} \texorpdfstring{$>$}{>}= 0x01000102

For more information, see hotplug. \mbox{\Hypertarget{libusb_8h_a291d7463aefd0de6209b537db4d06e70}\label{libusb_8h_a291d7463aefd0de6209b537db4d06e70}} 
\index{libusb.h@{libusb.h}!libusb\_pollfd\_added\_cb@{libusb\_pollfd\_added\_cb}}
\index{libusb\_pollfd\_added\_cb@{libusb\_pollfd\_added\_cb}!libusb.h@{libusb.h}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{libusb\_pollfd\_added\_cb}{libusb\_pollfd\_added\_cb}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily typedef \mbox{\hyperlink{libusb_8h_a8ca3594d1761da8da91be2851f4e8f21}{void}}(\mbox{\hyperlink{libusb_8h_aa7d6035eb2692d455d27144560a0f68d}{LIBUSB\+\_\+\+CALL}} $\ast$ libusb\+\_\+pollfd\+\_\+added\+\_\+cb) (int fd, short events, \mbox{\hyperlink{libusb_8h_a8ca3594d1761da8da91be2851f4e8f21}{void}} $\ast$user\+\_\+data)}

\mbox{\Hypertarget{libusb_8h_abff1d67f33725c93ef6dff699335c225}\label{libusb_8h_abff1d67f33725c93ef6dff699335c225}}

\index{libusb\_log\_level@{libusb\_log\_level}!libusb.h@{libusb.h}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{libusb\_log\_level}{libusb\_log\_level}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily enum \mbox{\hyperlink{libusb_8h_a2d6144203f0fc6d373677f6e2e89d2d2}{libusb\+\_\+log\+\_\+level}}}

Log message levels.
\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item LIBUSB\+\_\+\+LOG\+\_\+\+LEVEL\+\_\+\+NONE (0) \+: no messages ever printed by the library (default)
\item LIBUSB\+\_\+\+LOG\+\_\+\+LEVEL\+\_\+\+ERROR (1) \+: error messages are printed to stderr
\item LIBUSB\+\_\+\+LOG\+\_\+\+LEVEL\+\_\+\+WARNING (2) \+: warning and error messages are printed to stderr
\item LIBUSB\+\_\+\+LOG\+\_\+\+LEVEL\+\_\+\+INFO (3) \+: informational messages are printed to stdout, warning and error messages are printed to stderr
\item LIBUSB\+\_\+\+LOG\+\_\+\+LEVEL\+\_\+\+DEBUG (4) \+: debug and informational messages are printed to stdout, warnings and errors to stderr 
\end{DoxyItemize}\begin{DoxyEnumFields}{Enumerator}
\raisebox{\heightof{T}}[0pt][0pt]{\index{LIBUSB\_LOG\_LEVEL\_NONE@{LIBUSB\_LOG\_LEVEL\_NONE}!libusb.h@{libusb.h}}\index{libusb.h@{libusb.h}!LIBUSB\_LOG\_LEVEL\_NONE@{LIBUSB\_LOG\_LEVEL\_NONE}}}\mbox{\Hypertarget{libusb_8h_a2d6144203f0fc6d373677f6e2e89d2d2af431dbe84c85599526cc0103f8178270}\label{libusb_8h_a2d6144203f0fc6d373677f6e2e89d2d2af431dbe84c85599526cc0103f8178270}}

{\footnotesize\ttfamily enum \mbox{\hyperlink{libusb_8h_a1fb47dd0f7c209b60a3609ff0c03d56d}{libusb\+\_\+transfer\+\_\+flags}}}

\mbox{\hyperlink{structlibusb__transfer_ae26c063df30c2e29835212aad98c6e06}{libusb\+\_\+transfer.\+flags}} values \begin{DoxyEnumFields}{Enumerator}
\raisebox{\heightof{T}}[0pt][0pt]{\index{LIBUSB\_TRANSFER\_SHORT\_NOT\_OK@{LIBUSB\_TRANSFER\_SHORT\_NOT\_OK}!libusb.h@{libusb.h}}\index{libusb.h@{libusb.h}!LIBUSB\_TRANSFER\_SHORT\_NOT\_OK@{LIBUSB\_TRANSFER\_SHORT\_NOT\_OK}}}\mbox{\Hypertarget{libusb_8h_a1fb47dd0f7c209b60a3609ff0c03d56dae4c0697c266819c51c1734b3456e7276}\label{libusb_8h_a1fb47dd0f7c209b60a3609ff0c03d56dae4c0697c266819c51c1734b3456e7276}}

LIBUSB\+\_\+\+TRANSFER\+\_\+\+FREE\+\_\+\+BUFFER&Automatically free() transfer buffer during \mbox{\hyperlink{libusb_8h_a34956216e994484c68e17ff522d58cfd}{libusb\+\_\+free\+\_\+transfer()}} \\

\raisebox{\heightof{T}}[0pt][0pt]{\index{LIBUSB\_TRANSFER\_FREE\_TRANSFER@{LIBUSB\_TRANSFER\_FREE\_TRANSFER}!libusb.h@{libusb.h}}\index{libusb.h@{libusb.h}!LIBUSB\_TRANSFER\_FREE\_TRANSFER@{LIBUSB\_TRANSFER\_FREE\_TRANSFER}}}\mbox{\Hypertarget{libusb_8h_a1fb47dd0f7c209b60a3609ff0c03d56dacf3f064997b283a14097c9f4d6f8ccc1}\label{libusb_8h_a1fb47dd0f7c209b60a3609ff0c03d56dacf3f064997b283a14097c9f4d6f8ccc1}} 
LIBUSB\+\_\+\+TRANSFER\+\_\+\+FREE\+\_\+\+TRANSFER&Automatically call \mbox{\hyperlink{libusb_8h_a34956216e994484c68e17ff522d58cfd}{libusb\+\_\+free\+\_\+transfer()}} after callback returns. If this flag is set, it is illegal to call \mbox{\hyperlink{libusb_8h_a34956216e994484c68e17ff522d58cfd}{libusb\+\_\+free\+\_\+transfer()}} from your transfer callback, as this will result in a double-\/free when this flag is acted upon. \\
\hline

\raisebox{\heightof{T}}[0pt][0pt]{\index{LIBUSB\_TRANSFER\_ADD\_ZERO\_PACKET@{LIBUSB\_TRANSFER\_ADD\_ZERO\_PACKET}!libusb.h@{libusb.h}}\index{libusb.h@{libusb.h}!LIBUSB\_TRANSFER\_ADD\_ZERO\_PACKET@{LIBUSB\_TRANSFER\_ADD\_ZERO\_PACKET}}}\mbox{\Hypertarget{libusb_8h_a1fb47dd0f7c209b60a3609ff0c03d56da26b66334b6ec0537c49841ca623d901f}\label{libusb_8h_a1fb47dd0f7c209b60a3609ff0c03d56da26b66334b6ec0537c49841ca623d901f}} 
LIBUSB\+\_\+\+TRANSFER\+\_\+\+ADD\+\_\+\+ZERO\+\_\+\+PACKET&Terminate transfers that are a multiple of the endpoint\textquotesingle{}s w\+Max\+Packet\+Size with an extra zero length packet. This is useful when a device protocol mandates that each logical request is terminated by an incomplete packet (i.\+e. the logical requests are not separated by other means).

This flag only affects host-\/to-\/device transfers to bulk and interrupt endpoints. In other situations, it is ignored.

This flag only affects transfers with a length that is a multiple of the endpoint\textquotesingle{}s w\+Max\+Packet\+Size. On transfers of other lengths, this flag has no effect. Therefore, if you are working with a device that needs a ZLP whenever the end of the logical request falls on a packet boundary, then it is sensible to set this flag on {\itshape every} transfer (you do not have to worry about only setting it on transfers that end on the boundary).

This flag is currently only supported on Linux. On other systems, \mbox{\hyperlink{libusb_8h_a1efa266ce465fb51a2395feb4c4a9ad5}{libusb\+\_\+submit\+\_\+transfer()}} will return LIBUSB\+\_\+\+ERROR\+\_\+\+NOT\+\_\+\+SUPPORTED for every transfer where this flag is set.

Available since libusb-\/1.\+0.\+9. \\
\hline

\end{DoxyEnumFields}

\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{libusb\_hotplug\_deregister\_callback()}{libusb\_hotplug\_deregister\_callback()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \mbox{\hyperlink{libusb_8h_a8ca3594d1761da8da91be2851f4e8f21}{void}} \mbox{\hyperlink{libusb_8h_aa7d6035eb2692d455d27144560a0f68d}{LIBUSB\+\_\+\+CALL}} libusb\+\_\+hotplug\+\_\+deregister\+\_\+callback (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{libusb_8h_a4ec088aa7b79c4a9599e39bf36a72833}{libusb\+\_\+context}} $\ast$}]{ctx,  }\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{libusb_8h_a4868157346bbf2c70b6af0cb0a6c0094}{libusb\+\_\+hotplug\+\_\+callback\+\_\+handle}}}]{handle }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

Deregisters a hotplug callback.

Deregister a callback from a libusb\+\_\+context. This function is safe to call from within a hotplug callback.

Since version 1.\+0.\+16, \mbox{\hyperlink{libusb_8h_aa83ecded256e0767220bcc21cc92365d}{LIBUSBX\+\_\+\+API\+\_\+\+VERSION}} \texorpdfstring{$>$}{>}= 0x01000102


\begin{DoxyParams}[1]{Parameters}
\mbox{\texttt{ in}}  & {\em ctx} & context this callback is registered with \\
\hline
\mbox{\texttt{ in}}  & {\em handle} & the handle of the callback to deregister \\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}
\mbox{\Hypertarget{libusb_8h_a54961ed4615afb54c8cf50236b2e40d0}\label{libusb_8h_a54961ed4615afb54c8cf50236b2e40d0}} 
\index{libusb.h@{libusb.h}!libusb\_hotplug\_register\_callback@{libusb\_hotplug\_register\_callback}}
\index{libusb\_hotplug\_register\_callback@{libusb\_hotplug\_register\_callback}!libusb.h@{libusb.h}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{libusb\_hotplug\_register\_callback()}{libusb\_hotplug\_register\_callback()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily int \mbox{\hyperlink{libusb_8h_aa7d6035eb2692d455d27144560a0f68d}{LIBUSB\+\_\+\+CALL}} libusb\+\_\+hotplug\+\_\+register\+\_\+callback (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{libusb_8h_a4ec088aa7b79c4a9599e39bf36a72833}{libusb\+\_\+context}} $\ast$}]{ctx,  }\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{libusb_8h_a556d598ca379618a41bbec3597f55dcf}{libusb\+\_\+hotplug\+\_\+event}}}]{events,  }\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{libusb_8h_a95ce2ec85dec177854c423cea2853c52}{libusb\+\_\+hotplug\+\_\+flag}}}]{flags,  }\item[{int}]{vendor\+\_\+id,  }\item[{int}]{product\+\_\+id,  }\item[{int}]{dev\+\_\+class,  }\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{libusb_8h_a34e9904eb8e5124057a866f777cc99a8}{libusb\+\_\+hotplug\+\_\+callback\+\_\+fn}}}]{cb\+\_\+fn,  }\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{libusb_8h_a8ca3594d1761da8da91be2851f4e8f21}{void}} $\ast$}]{user\+\_\+data,  }\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{libusb_8h_a4868157346bbf2c70b6af0cb0a6c0094}{libusb\+\_\+hotplug\+\_\+callback\+\_\+handle}} $\ast$}]{handle }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

Register a hotplug callback function

Register a callback with the libusb\+\_\+context. The callback will fire when a matching event occurs on a matching device. The callback is armed until either it is deregistered with \mbox{\hyperlink{libusb_8h_afe4401894825a2671daa78cbf7094f55}{libusb\+\_\+hotplug\+\_\+deregister\+\_\+callback()}} or the supplied callback returns 1 to indicate it is finished processing events.

If the \mbox{\hyperlink{libusb_8h_a95ce2ec85dec177854c423cea2853c52a01a1c0c9f4e6852cb6df713f2e8a7f6b}{LIBUSB\+\_\+\+HOTPLUG\+\_\+\+ENUMERATE}} is passed the callback will be called with a \mbox{\hyperlink{libusb_8h_a556d598ca379618a41bbec3597f55dcfac012270cba6e08dafe7e3bec204dffd6}{LIBUSB\+\_\+\+HOTPLUG\+\_\+\+EVENT\+\_\+\+DEVICE\+\_\+\+ARRIVED}} for all devices already plugged into the machine. Note that libusbx modifies its internal device list from a separate thread, while calling hotplug callbacks from \mbox{\hyperlink{libusb_8h_a6959bab068afc01988f851144ebc8a85}{libusb\+\_\+handle\+\_\+events()}}, so it is possible for a device to already be present on, or removed from, its internal device list, while the hotplug callbacks still need to be dispatched. This means that when using \mbox{\hyperlink{libusb_8h_a95ce2ec85dec177854c423cea2853c52a01a1c0c9f4e6852cb6df713f2e8a7f6b}{LIBUSB\+\_\+\+HOTPLUG\+\_\+\+ENUMERATE}}, your callback may be called twice for the arrival of the same device, once from \mbox{\hyperlink{libusb_8h_a54961ed4615afb54c8cf50236b2e40d0}{libusb\+\_\+hotplug\+\_\+register\+\_\+callback()}} and once from \mbox{\hyperlink{libusb_8h_a6959bab068afc01988f851144ebc8a85}{libusb\+\_\+handle\+\_\+events()}}; and/or your callback may be called for the removal of a device for which an arrived call was never made.

Since version 1.\+0.\+16, \mbox{\hyperlink{libusb_8h_aa83ecded256e0767220bcc21cc92365d}{LIBUSBX\+\_\+\+API\+\_\+\+VERSION}} \texorpdfstring{$>$}{>}= 0x01000102


\begin{DoxyParams}[1]{Parameters}
\mbox{\texttt{ in}}  & {\em ctx} & context to register this callback with \\
\hline
\mbox{\texttt{ in}}  & {\em events} & bitwise or of events that will trigger this callback. See \mbox{\hyperlink{libusb_8h_a556d598ca379618a41bbec3597f55dcf}{libusb\+\_\+hotplug\+\_\+event}} \\
\hline
\mbox{\texttt{ in}}  & {\em flags} & hotplug callback flags. See \mbox{\hyperlink{libusb_8h_a95ce2ec85dec177854c423cea2853c52}{libusb\+\_\+hotplug\+\_\+flag}} \\
\hline
\mbox{\texttt{ in}}  & {\em vendor\+\_\+id} & the vendor id to match or \mbox{\hyperlink{libusb_8h_a6d4f5e524a3b7ab4a25b751073335d4c}{LIBUSB\+\_\+\+HOTPLUG\+\_\+\+MATCH\+\_\+\+ANY}} \\
\hline
\mbox{\texttt{ in}}  & {\em product\+\_\+id} & the product id to match or \mbox{\hyperlink{libusb_8h_a6d4f5e524a3b7ab4a25b751073335d4c}{LIBUSB\+\_\+\+HOTPLUG\+\_\+\+MATCH\+\_\+\+ANY}} \\
\hline
\mbox{\texttt{ in}}  & {\em dev\+\_\+class} & the device class to match or \mbox{\hyperlink{libusb_8h_a6d4f5e524a3b7ab4a25b751073335d4c}{LIBUSB\+\_\+\+HOTPLUG\+\_\+\+MATCH\+\_\+\+ANY}} \\
\hline
\mbox{\texttt{ in}}  & {\em cb\+\_\+fn} & the function to be invoked on a matching event/device \\
\hline
\mbox{\texttt{ in}}  & {\em user\+\_\+data} & user data to pass to the callback function \\
\hline
\mbox{\texttt{ out}}  & {\em handle} & pointer to store the handle of the allocated callback (can be NULL) \\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
LIBUSB\+\_\+\+SUCCESS on success LIBUSB\+\_\+\+ERROR code on failure 
\end{DoxyReturn}

\mbox{\Hypertarget{libusb_8h_a8ca3594d1761da8da91be2851f4e8f21}\label{libusb_8h_a8ca3594d1761da8da91be2851f4e8f21}} 
\index{libusb.h@{libusb.h}!void@{void}}
\index{void@{void}!libusb.h@{libusb.h}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{void()}{void()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily typedef void (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{libusb_8h_aa7d6035eb2692d455d27144560a0f68d}{LIBUSB\+\_\+\+CALL}} $\ast$}]{libusb\+\_\+transfer\+\_\+cb\+\_\+fn }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

Asynchronous transfer callback function type. When submitting asynchronous transfers, you pass a pointer to a callback function of this type via the \mbox{\hyperlink{structlibusb__transfer_a69c6df011ec23ff3e481cc98bfff0623}{callback}} member of the \mbox{\hyperlink{structlibusb__transfer}{libusb\+\_\+transfer}} structure. libusbx will call this function later, when the transfer has completed or failed. See asyncio for more information. 
\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
{\em transfer} & The \mbox{\hyperlink{structlibusb__transfer}{libusb\+\_\+transfer}} struct the callback function is being notified about. \\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}
